< username>

<userid>105635371387326881884</userid>< Text>
Shell Shock ruined my Valentine's Day.

My husband and I ran across Shell Shock on Yelp when looking for a place to have our Valentine's Day dinner. We checked out their website, saw that they had a daily happy hour and that their rice bowls looked good and thought hey - oysters sound like a fun option. Let's do that.

Wow, did we make a bad decision. Immediately after we made a reservation online, we were contacted for our credit card number; if we chose to cancel our reservation within 24 hours of Valentine's Day, it would be charged. Okay, fair enough, we can understand that.

AT NO POINT did anyone mention the required prix fixe - it was not posted online, nor did they mention the prix fixe when they called to confirm our reservation. We didn't realize there was a prix fixe until we were seated at the restaurant; we were trapped.

Well, we thought to ourselves, maybe it will be worth it. Let's give it a chance.

The prix fixe $75 was for 3 courses, no drinks included. I'm lactose intolerant and couldn't eat any of the desserts. The waiter worked with us to reduce the price of my meal to $65. I paid $65 for 4 oysters and a mediocre cioppino in which all of the seafood was overcooked. My husband was a happier with his meal - he got oysters, rib-eye, and chocolate cake - all of which were serviceable, but certainly NOT worth the price. But then, he felt sick all of the following day; we suspect it was something he ate. The wine was the best part of our meal, but even that wasn't stellar. We left the restaurant and spent the rest of the evening angry.

We contacted the restaurant privately to share our poor experience and frustrations and have not received a response. Deceitful business practices and second-rate food? You can do better at most other restaurants on Castro Street. Definitely avoid Shell Shock.</Text>

<user>108055488577998396055</user><user_name>Debbie Hughes</user_name><Date>1553377071232< /Date>< rating>

< text>
I have taken my Dog "Buzzy" and Cats to Rocklin Road Animal Hospital for many years. The reason I feel compelled to write this is because I want my Friends in the community to have the facts to make the best decision for their Pets. I have no hard feelings towards the Associate Vets or the Staff, everyone is great!. To set the stage, A few years back I was shocked that I was being charged 30 dollars to have my Cat's blood pressure checked, Who does that?. That was a small red flag, but I let it go. However, the main issue is they call their clinic a "Veterinary Hospital" but do not have state of the art equipment. Many procedures cannot be done and are referred out, or a specialist comes in, for example to do an Ultrasound. What happened to me is I took my sick French Bulldog "Buzzy" in as he was not doing well. The Vet charged me over $700.00 and then sent him home the same day. My Dog was so sick that he could not stand up and fell over when I took him outside to go to the bathroom. The next morning, I rushed "Buzzy" to Loomis Basin Animal Hospital, The Vet on staff did an emergency Ultrasound on him. They found a tumor mass on his heart and immediately sat me down to tell me that "Buzzy" was a "Very Sick Dog". The best option was to put him down and put him out of his misery and that's what I sadly did. A few weeks later, I reached out to Dr. Grunder about this and felt I should be refunded for "Buzzy's" $700.00 Visit. I was naturally emotional and felt Dr. Grunder was somewhat apprehensive to make things right. I ended up with a refund under 200 dollars. In retrospect, I feel this was a token, so I recently wrote him a letter asking for a full refund for not diagnosing my Dog correctly and sending him home sick. I decided to do this because I feel a full refund is the right thing to do. I have not heard back from him. (I'am still paying off this bill and the second bill from Loomis Basin). So this is just a heads-up that if things do not go well and your animal is very sick, You may end up going to another Vet and incurring another bill. If your Dog is very ill, consider taking him to an Animal Hospital that has all the necessary state of the art equipment. This could save your Dog or Cat's life or save them from suffering. This can also save you from personal and financial anguish. On a positive note, the routine care at Rocklin Road Hospital was very good. The Vets and Dr. Williams are super kind and the Vet Techs and staff are very nice as well.< /text>

<Text>3.5/5. Huku is like that weird uncle or cousin that has the hip new gadgets at Christmas but is not really that awesome or memorable. Although it has a shiny exterior and cool combinations, the sushi here is pretty average.

I've came for dinner and lunch. At dinner I used a $20 off $50 coupon. I tried the Rock N Roll and tuna tataki salad. My friend had some deep fried role and chicken Katsu. The rock n roll tried to be cool by mixing different fish and having a spicy mayo dipping sauce, but the flavors were generally lacking and fish quality was only ok. The tuna tataki was also rather bland, I did like the shredded beets in the salad.

The lunch bento box was slightly better, with good beef teriyaki, a nice croquette, and sweet potato ball thing. The miso soup was good. The tuna however was just ok. With just ok fish and forgettable combinations, this place is just ok and there's lots of better options in Davis.< /Text><pics>None<//pics>< Response>

Merry Contrary<//name>
<userid>116624701880308242907<//userid>< Review>
It's a Saturday night, and the only people here are me and my husband.

It seems that most people take out, and given the lack of air conditioning, I can see why.

Service is spotty at best, but perhaps it's because of all the takeout orders.

My husband had the hot and sour soup, while I had egg rolls as an appetizer. Both were delicious.

For the main course, we settled on orange chicken and teriyaki beef.  The orange chicken was absolutely delicious and the orange sauce was light and not overbearing.

I felt the teriyaki beef was a little too salty but my husband enjoyed it. If I was rating this restaurant purely on food, I would give it 5 stars, but the service, or lack thereof, is why I'm only giving it 4 stars.

Will I return? Much of that depends on how much we enjoy the leftovers in the next few days. However, if we do return it will only be for takeout from now on.< /Review>

< review>
The place always looks closed and I think I'm the only one who eats there - everyone else seems to do takeout.  Ambiance is lacking - the place looks old and tired.  Service is OK as long as you don't mind limited English speakers with VERY thick accents.

The pork fried rice is really great.  Also, paper wrapped chicken is a decent chuck of chicken.  A lot of places give you a pathetic scrap of meat inside that 400 degree aluminum foil.

Prices are good, beverage selection is poor.</review>

< review>
The ER team at Mercy Folsom is consistently exceptional. Kindness, and compassion do not vary no matter how busy they are. Over the years, the triage process has improved, and so has the patient experience especially for wait times. It is however an ER, and as such, you may have to wait so that they can treat those with a greater need. Fortunately,  or unfortunately, over the years, I have had to visit quite a few times in a personal or community outreach capacity. My thanks to the Cummings family and their generosity for the new ER pavilion.< /review>

<time>1564993237640<//time><Rating>5</Rating>< review>
Mercy hospital emergency room treated by broken arm on 2000-01-02 when I crashed a mountain bicycle deep in the woods between Folsom Point (Formerly Dyke 8) and the Brown's Ravine Recreational Area.  Emergency rooms get pretty busy around holidays, so it should come as no surprise that a broken arm waited several hours while more serious injuries were being tended.  A merciful angel heard my whimpering and made me comfortable with Morphine until I was seen, X-rayed, treated, and my partner got me home.  Thank you for being there on the holiday weekend when the rest of us were out finding ways to need you.  Mercy Hospital of Folsom is a Blessing in Folsom...</review>

<Date>1571764873492< /Date><name>Paris J<//name>< Review>
While in the emergency room, the attending nurse (I believe her name was Sarah) tried to put my IV in and then attempted to push the medication. After I pulled my arm back due to the pain, she stated "oh that hurts huh" I then advised her it did. She had to then start on my other arm. I was there for dehydration and a migraine, I have been there for the same exact thing before a few short months prior. I was given all of my medications within a 1.5 to 2 minute span, I was nervous about this as the last time I was advised that reglan had to be pushed through extremely slow. Within minutes I felt very anxious, one moment I was sitting up, the next moment I was unconscious. I woke up panicking and crying, the nurse didn't have me hooked up to anything that was monitoring what was happening to me. I called for the first person I saw, she tried to help me but I couldn't explain anything, I couldn't breathe. I passed out again and woke back up it was only 2-3 seconds but was enough to send me into a full blown panic attack. I started seizing and they started to go get the doctor. I stopped seizing for 1-2 minutes and started seizing again. I came out of the seizure still panicking, the doctor really helped a lot to calm me down but I couldn't get over the overwhelming feeling that I was going to die. I was feeling very anxious and there was nothing that was done by "my" nurse that made me feel better but she also didn't seem like she cared very much. They hooked me up to the monitors after my episodes. My heart rate started accelerating greatly and the machine went off, no one came. I pushed the call button, no one came. My heart rate went higher, the machine continued to go off, no one came. I pushed the button again twice more about 2-3 minutes apart, no one came. I had to call out for help and my nurse stated "you're fine I just have to adjust the parameters everything looks fine". I could clearly see my pulse was over 130 and my BP was high. I wanted to go home the entire time, I was sent home about 45 minutes later with no medication instructions. I've never had a panic attack, a seizure, or loss of consciousness... that day I had all 3. I'm aware that these can be side affects of the medication but I can't help but feel that it would have never happened if the nurse did her job and pushed the medication slower instead of rushing. I am suffering from anxiety every time I think about the situation and am extremely afraid to go back to the E.R.</Review>

I was a patient at the hospital from Monday night, 8/26 to Thursday afternoon, 8/29.
I have never had a more positive and satisfying hospital stay in my life.  I have been in other hospitals and I can safely say, the service and professionalism of this staff is the most impressive.

Personnel

My care staff included Nurses, Marichou, Rizza, Christina, Pasanyit, Miao and Vandara and Doctor Sidici.  All were excellent but Marichou, Pasanyit and Vandara went beyond in providing care, concern and interest.  I wish to thank all of them.

Food

The kitchen did an excellent job of providing favorable and tasty things to eat.  They were responsive to specific requests.  An example, I asked to have yogurt and hot sauce added to my menu for the next day.  Out of concern I might want it that evening, they made a special trip after hours to deliver not long after I hung up the phone.  Great Service.

Management

I have never had a Nurse Supervisor come to my room and ask if the level of service is satisfactory, but I did at Mercy Folsom.  I am impressed with their attitude, We Care.

It comes through everything and was a welcome surprise.

Cleanliness

The person tasked with cleaning the room, Sergio, did a marvelous job.  He was patient with me when I asked about cleaning supplies and equipment used.  He like the rest of the staff displayed the We Care attitude.

Summary

There is no part of my experience that was less than superb.  You are a class act Mercy Hospital of Folsom.  If asked, I will refer others to you.

< review>
I brought my wife here at the direction of our family doctor because she was having severe pain around her kidneys and abdomen.  The experience in the ER was good.  They took CT scans and did an ultrasound.  Her white blood cell count was way up.  They couldn't figure out what was causing the pain so they decided to admit her.  That's when the experience took a horrible turn.  The nurses in the hospital are really bad.  It's as though they are going through the motions required of the profession, but without any empathy, listening skills, or genuine care for the patients whatsoever.  They smile when they introduce themselves but as soon as you start asking questions or try to tell them what your concerns are they go into a defensive posture and are almost combative, in a passive-aggressive sort of way.  It was pervasive throughout the culture there.  I kept asking for ice packs for my wife when they would melt or leak and the nurses seemed really put out by it.  I told them I would happily refill them myself if there was an ice machine somewhere, but I was told I could not.  The bathroom for our shared room ran out of paper towels on day one, and after three requests by day two the paper towel dispenser was still empty.  They told me they didn't have access to the janitorial supplies.  The horror of the experience came to a head around noon on the second day.  The night before we had told the nurse that the morphine they were giving her wasn't working for very long but the Toradol (non narcotic NSAID) they had given her seemed to work better.  The nurse said the doctor had only authorized one dose of the Toradol.  So at 2:30am she refused the morphine because it wasn't working and made her nauseous.  She refused it again at 6:30am but at 7am she accepted it because she was in tons of pain.  around 11 she asked if there was anything else they could give her for the pain.  The doctor came in at that point (hadn't seen him at all yet and had no idea what the treatment plan was or if there was one, although we had been asking).  The doctor informed her that "the computer had flagged her as drug seeking" and she couldn't have anything else for her pain and they wanted to discharge her because they couldn't find the source of the pain.  Keep in mind her white blood cell count had been very high and had come down with antibiotics.  So she had something going on, they just couldn't figure out what.  Anyway, I freaked out at that point.  The horrible nurses and now the doctor accusing my wife of being drug seeking was just too much.  I called our family doctor (who was also furious) and asked him for help.  He called the hospital and asked for the doctor to return his call, but the doctor never called him back (even three days later after multiple messages and pages).  His name is Dr. Kanwaljit Kahlon.  I can only say that in my experience with him his is without a doubt the worst doctor I have ever encountered.  If you can imagine your loved one crying because he/she was accused of being an addict and seeking narcotics, while he/she was enduring terrible pain and the uncertainty of not knowing what is wrong, you can begin to relate to the distaste I have for this man.  In conclusion, after the doctor left and I told the charge nurse what I thought of their staff, they quickly discharged my wife without any direction as to follow up care, even though they had given her two days of antibiotics and her white blood cell count had come down substantially.  The following day we went to our family doctor, who thought that we should finish a course of antibiotics that was started in case it was a kidney infection and assured her that if the pain didn't improve then we would explore other options (ischemic bowel, other possible kidney issues, etc.).  It was the first assurance we received from a doctor about a plan for trying to understand her situation since we left emergency.  Our time at that hospital was gut-wrenching in more ways than one and I wouldn't wish it on anyone.  Please avoid.< /review>

<user_id>105213255561655655900< /user_id><user_name>Brendon Nemeth< /user_name><Time>1589250998301<//Time><Rate>5< /Rate><Text>Had a reservation for a 5x11 but found a better deal for a 5x15 online. I made the reservation for the new 5x15 as well, since why wouldn't we want more space for less money? I called the office and spoke to the manager, Lee, who explained to me the reason for the special low price was that it is actually three 5x5s side-by-side with the middle walls knocked out. So instead of your typical 5ft. wide and 15ft. deep, it goes only 5ft. deep and 15ft. wide (across). Other drawback was that there are 3 separate doors, all needing individual locks.***

We decided to keep both reservations so we could see both units and make a decision from there. They told me that only one person was allowed in the office at a time, and face-coverings were required (good). When we arrived, Lee informed us that despite our reservation, there were no 5x11s left, only 5x10. After looking at the units, we decided that the extra space at the better deal was worth having to deal with multiple doors/locks, and went with the 5x15.

They have carts available to use that are generally available depending on how many people are there. The lights are all on sensors, so while it seems dark, things light up as you walk. The floors are soft and smooth which makes a big difference after storing somewhere that had very loud and uneven floors.

To access our building, you do have to get out of your car to enter the code into the intercom box, which is a negative. The convenience and security of being able to pull up and enter your code from your vehicle makes a difference, especially for my wife feeling safe if she is going alone.

They have security cameras covering the gate entrance/exit area, but nothing once you get further in. Part of me wishes they had more coverage once inside, but their reason of protecting people's privacy also makes some sense.

The units themselves seem very secure. Our last place we ended up having to get a collapsable shower rod and curtain to hang on the inside because you could see through the sides of the doors right into the unit. This Public Storage does not have that issue, which is really nice and comforting. There is a steel mesh type cover over the top in our building, which seems secure so people don't come through the top.

Overall we are happy with our move and decision to switch to Public Storage. This location is convenient off the freeway and we feel comfortable with the security of our stuff. Lee was very nice and easy to work with. From what I've gathered, she has been the manager there for 10+ years and runs the show for all things logistics and security.

The process of doing all the paperwork and setting everything up was very quick, smooth, and easy. They were very cautious about staying a good distance form each other and even made my wife stay outside initially until they let her come in and stand in the far corner (lol). We felt safe and comfortable the whole time which was important to our experience and desire to stat long-term. They have an ongoing deal for $1 first month's rent and 15%-30% off rent if booked online.

We plan to stay here for as long as possible until they raise our rent to the point where it's unaffordable and we have to move on. Hoping that doesn't happen! Thanks again Lee and the rest of the PS B-Game staff!

***NOTE: They use special bolt-style locks that are specifically designed for their storage doors, meaning you have to purchase a lock through them ($20/ea). If you have your own pad lock, you can use that as additional security, but their lock is required to store there.</Text><Pictures>[{'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipMZsAIfvIweV41oMvgNMBy-3HOX2hwYkAkW26ii=w150-h150-k-no-p']}, {'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipNLwPv84NXML8Gt7DH7Gwol778stV0KnlANkp1K=w150-h150-k-no-p']}, {'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipOa9vKiQNVSkI1iB3taO4cIGpEXpvFlOyi1nznc=w150-h150-k-no-p']}, {'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipMRVFRdvfz7ZTTtN_gWj4oKzZ7GBl1q_bVzrBdD=w150-h150-k-no-p']}, {'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipMSzw7D3KH2cuseL_V6GTc-y-4LIyxLQgMgtTvp=w150-h150-k-no-p']}, {'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipO7fUMOk6ykL3o70oAgO0JEXW9TyiRteUQYleKg=w150-h150-k-no-p']}, {'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipMxm-mGbXFS624Kdq4p5fEdgC-IGA-98PDGF6Mc=w150-h150-k-no-p']}, {'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipNbqzTLHxt8d1I8tp_jF7o24lg5VqgMQDgtj-JH=w150-h150-k-no-p']}, {'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipMC8riP0VMaEznmxPDurZ91kYwpLLom-vYCHx6s=w150-h150-k-no-p']}, {'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipOD6YdHZzHcI1UeXubUgI9vlvoYyb-fkQkW-Hzj=w150-h150-k-no-p']}]< /Pictures>< Resp>

<review>Had a reservation for a 5x11 but found a better deal for a 5x15 online. I made the reservation for the new 5x15 as well, since why wouldn't we want more space for less money? I called the office and spoke to the manager, Lee, who explained to me the reason for the special low price was that it is actually three 5x5s side-by-side with the middle walls knocked out. So instead of your typical 5ft. wide and 15ft. deep, it goes only 5ft. deep and 15ft. wide (across). Other drawback was that there are 3 separate doors, all needing individual locks.***

We decided to keep both reservations so we could see both units and make a decision from there. They told me that only one person was allowed in the office at a time, and face-coverings were required (good). When we arrived, Lee informed us that despite our reservation, there were no 5x11s left, only 5x10. After looking at the units, we decided that the extra space at the better deal was worth having to deal with multiple doors/locks, and went with the 5x15.

They have carts available to use that are generally available depending on how many people are there. The lights are all on sensors, so while it seems dark, things light up as you walk. The floors are soft and smooth which makes a big difference after storing somewhere that had very loud and uneven floors.

To access our building, you do have to get out of your car to enter the code into the intercom box, which is a negative. The convenience and security of being able to pull up and enter your code from your vehicle makes a difference, especially for my wife feeling safe if she is going alone.

They have security cameras covering the gate entrance/exit area, but nothing once you get further in. Part of me wishes they had more coverage once inside, but their reason of protecting people's privacy also makes some sense.

The units themselves seem very secure. Our last place we ended up having to get a collapsable shower rod and curtain to hang on the inside because you could see through the sides of the doors right into the unit. This Public Storage does not have that issue, which is really nice and comforting. There is a steel mesh type cover over the top in our building, which seems secure so people don't come through the top.

Overall we are happy with our move and decision to switch to Public Storage. This location is convenient off the freeway and we feel comfortable with the security of our stuff. Lee was very nice and easy to work with. From what I've gathered, she has been the manager there for 10+ years and runs the show for all things logistics and security.

The process of doing all the paperwork and setting everything up was very quick, smooth, and easy. They were very cautious about staying a good distance form each other and even made my wife stay outside initially until they let her come in and stand in the far corner (lol). We felt safe and comfortable the whole time which was important to our experience and desire to stat long-term. They have an ongoing deal for $1 first month's rent and 15%-30% off rent if booked online.

We plan to stay here for as long as possible until they raise our rent to the point where it's unaffordable and we have to move on. Hoping that doesn't happen! Thanks again Lee and the rest of the PS B-Game staff!

<resp>None<//resp>< Text>
I'll be honest - upon initial research, I had my doubts because it's very hard for any product/service/company to consistently maintain such a near-perfect rating for hundreds of reviews. However, after making a reservation and going through the Burlingame facility myself, I'm now 1000% confident as to why!

We were in a pickle as we ran out of space on the day before our move-out. Literally within minutes of placing the reservation online for the same day only 2.5 hours before closing, Bruce called me to confirm and walked through all the details. Bruce was very considerate of our time on the phone and extremely friendly while walking us through the reservation details and check-in process - he even warned us about the notorious red light cameras on Millbrae Ave on the way over that we've seen all too many people fall victim to (including our own friends haha).

Then when we arrived an hour later, like everyone else's reviews, Lee Ho was the absolute best at the front desk! She greeted us with a friendly smile and happily guided us through the first-time reservation process, standard procedures, where to go afterwards, etc. We felt bad because a line started to form because the first-time reservation process had a couple of things to read, sign, and type into their iPad, but Lee acknowledged and handled everyone behind us like a professional.

All in all, the Burlingame location being a very clean facility in a convenient location run by extremely great & friendly staff made us very happy with our experience!< /Text>

This place is super clean (literally SMELLS clean!) and is clearly well maintained. I checked into my unit for the first time today and had a great experience. <Text>Very disappointed with Public Storage unethical behavior during the current world health crisis.  I had originally begun using Public Storage due to their high rating, however, I've come to realize that all they care about is making a quick buck. Public Storage has decided to raise prices right as the COVID-19 crisis began to unfold, clearly taking advantage of the situation. They sent me a letter dated March 4th, 2020 that they will be raising prices. This is the second price hike within the last 12 month period. My original payments were $172 a month and have now been raised to $260 a month, that is a 51% increase in price within 1 year period.

The current health crisis has put me out of a job and I've been sheltered at home as mandated by the state. I've been cutting as many expenses as possible. When I called them to ask about holding off on price hikes until the crisis is over and I can get back to work, they told me that there's nothing they can do and they have to protect their business. If I'm unable to make payments they will sell off all my belongings. Most industries are coming together to help each other during the crisis. Banks are offering grace periods on loans, insurance companies are reducing and refunding premiums, however Public Storage has decided that it's in their best interest to raise prices right now, when people are most vulnerable and trapped in their homes.

Lastly, most of Public Storage 5 star reviews are bought by Public Storage when they are signing up new customers. They have special locks that they require for all their units that you have to buy from them for $20. They offer all new customers this lock for free during the signing process, if they write them a five star review and they verify the review is a positive 5 stars. They are basically bribing customers for reviews. How can someone give a good faith review with a storage business that they haven't even begun to use?<//Text>< gmap_id>

<UserId.>105655874960370304845< /UserId.><username>Dr. Flywheel< /username><time>1557778780601<//time><rate>4<//rate>< text>
Large and convenient self-storage facility with good access to its local neighborhoods. The facility is very clean inside, and is provided with good  security features, including coded elevator checks and access verification. I like that the facility is fully air conditioned, as is required for the hot months of the year, if you care about your "stuff" remaining in its original condition, while kept in your private storage cell. Modern security locks protect access to each door. The facility also provides special storage cell with means for easing access to stored content for people with physical disabilities. Note that this is a self-service facility and you are unlikely to see or get immediate help from any resident personnel. A on-way (out) emergency exit allows quick evacuation, if needed. Though I never actually checked that exit route in person.<//text>

<Gmap_id>0x808f77c9877a20fb:0x50d8dd2a669b2457</Gmap_id><userid>100279957443148833914<//userid><pictures>None</pictures>< Text>
Manager Lee Ho:

1) Harassed me whenever I was on property.
2) Essentially accused me of being homeless because of my frequent use of the facility.
3) Used the on-site security cameras and check-in system to stalk my vehicle and physical whereabouts.
4) Stated that the way my unit was organized was "inappropriate" and gave me four days to move out on the same day I had finally finished moving everything in.
5) Threatened to call police and have all of my belongings removed if I did not comply. A set of actions which does not abide by the general terms of the rental/lease agreement. All of her threats and accusations were made out of hostility and directed at me personally.

Fact is, I should've sued. I work three jobs and am in the process of moving from Hawaii to California. Not that my personal business is anyone else's business. Especially someone who brags about managing storage facilities for ten years. Which is nothing to brag about btw. I read all these 5-star reviews and can't help but think that interacting with a person once every six months hardly qualifies as an "experience."

I read a review where some people had their units looted and feel like I should mention that there were ACTUAL homeless people on property when I moved in. One day, I heard someone snoring two doors down from me. Never noticed any video cameras in the storage area. Not sure how Lee Ho was stalking me, but maybe if she used those cameras to catch thieves, those poor people would still have all their earthly possessions.

Great place. Brand new facility. Very affordable. Remainder of the staff - amazing and pleasant. I regret having to take my business elsewhere. I know I'm not alone since other 1-star reviews are different people who have also been mistreated by Lee Ho. While looking for another storage facility, I came across similar reviews about Lee Ho since she has managed almost every facility in a ten-mile radius. She conveniently failed to mention her lack of staying power and innate ability to openly discriminate against paying customers who break no rules. Clearly identifiable negative patterns are far more important than point of sale transactions/interactions.</Text>

1) Harassed me whenever I was on property.
2) Essentially accused me of being homeless because of my frequent use of the facility.
